# The Last Orbit - Full Draft

Document Type: novel_script

## Purpose
Develop a coherent full-length draft with stable character arcs, setting continuity, and event chronology for revision planning.

## Sections
### Act I - Departure
In Act I - Departure, case 1 tracks how Captain Mira handled docking dispute at Orion Station, emitted a distress beacon, and used continuity pass so character motivations stay consistent. At 05:11 UTC, reviewers checked character arc coverage, recorded an audit trail entry, and confirmed that the Orion Station decision remained consistent with prior sections. The team reconciled 746 affected units, compared timeline order against business order, and wrote a verification note linking the incident to Echo Gate criteria. A focused rehearsal evaluated fallback behavior, then documented how scene dependency mapping prevented regressions while keeping the narrative and operational intent readable. Stakeholders accepted this checkpoint after evidence review showed that distress beacon and owner actions were traceable, attributable, and aligned

with the stated purpose. Cross-functional discussion highlighted repeated phrases and entities, including Council Accord, so they could be tagged, searched, and reused in downstream verification steps. During validation, the group compared local findings with external references, then updated run notes to preserve continuity across edits and future reruns. This passage captures a concrete decision boundary: when uncertainty rose, teams escalated early, preserved context, and logged the exact rationale behind each change. By tying narrative details to machine-verifiable structure, the scenario proves that readable prose can coexist with deterministic storage and reconstruction rules.
